---
title: English Adjectives
description: A comprehensive list of common English adjectives with phonetic pronunciation, definitions, and example sentences
---

# abandoned

pho: /əˈbæn.dn̩d/
def: Left completely and no longer cared for
eg: The house was abandoned after the storm
eg: He felt abandoned by his friends

# able

pho: /ˈeɪ.bəl/
def: Having the skill, power, or opportunity to do something.
eg: She was able to finish the race despite the rain
eg: He’s not able to come to the meeting today

# absolute

pho: /ˈæb.sə.luːt/
def: Complete and total; not limited in any way.
eg: She has absolute confidence in her team
eg: The solution requires absolute precision

# academic

pho: /ˌæk.əˈdem.ɪk/
def: Related to education, study, or scholarly activity
eg: She joined the academic community after publishing her research
eg: He struggled with the academic requirements of the course

# acceptable

pho: /əkˈsep.tə.bəl/
def: Good enough to be allowed or approved
eg: The food quality was acceptable, but nothing special
eg: Your behavior was acceptable under the circumstances

# acclaimed

pho: /əˈkleɪmd/
def: Praised enthusiastically by many people
eg: The critically acclaimed film won several awards
eg: She’s an acclaimed author in the mystery genre

# accomplished

pho: /əˈkɒm.plɪʃt/
def: Highly skilled or successful at something
eg: He’s an accomplished pianist
eg: The accomplished surgeon performed the operation flawlessly

# accurate

pho: /ˈæk.jə.rət/
def: Correct and free from mistakes
eg: The measurements were accurate to within a millimeter
eg: She gave an accurate description of the event

# acidic

pho: /əˈsɪd.ɪk/
def: Having a sour or sharp taste; containing acid
eg: Lemon juice is very acidic
eg: The soil in this region is too acidic for most crops

# acrobatic

pho: /ˌæk.rəˈbæt.ɪk/
def: Involving impressive physical balance or agility
eg: The gymnast’s acrobatic routine thrilled the crowd
eg: The cat made an acrobatic leap onto the high shelf

# active

pho: /ˈæk.tɪv/
def: Engaging in action or movement; energetic or busy
def: Currently operating or in use
eg: She leads an active lifestyle, hiking and cycling most weekends
eg: The volcano is still active and could erupt at any time

# actual

pho: /ˈæk.tʃu.əl/
def: Real or existing in fact, not imagined or expected
eg: The actual cost was higher than we expected
eg: This is the actual reason for the delay

# adept

pho: /əˈdept/
def: Very skilled or proficient at something
eg: He is adept at solving complex problems
eg: She became adept with the new software quickly

# admirable

pho: /ˈæd.mə.rə.bəl/
def: Deserving respect or approval
eg: Her dedication to the project is admirable
eg: He showed admirable patience under pressure

# admired

pho: /ədˈmaɪrd/
def: Regarded with respect, approval, or affection
eg: She is admired by her colleagues
eg: The admired leader announced his retirement

# adolescent

pho: /ˌæd.əˈles.ənt/
def: Relating to the period between childhood and adulthood
eg: Adolescents often seek more independence
eg: The program is designed for adolescent students

# adorable

pho: /əˈdɔː.rə.bəl/
def: Very attractive or charming in a sweet way
eg: The puppy looks absolutely adorable
eg: She gave an adorable smile

# adored

pho: /əˈdɔːrd/
def: Loved deeply or intensely
eg: The singer is adored by her fans
eg: He was adored by everyone in the community

# advanced

pho: /ədˈvænst/
def: Highly developed or ahead in progress or knowledge
eg: This course covers advanced topics
eg: The hospital uses advanced medical technology

# adventurous

pho: /ədˈven.tʃə.rəs/
def: Willing to try new or exciting experiences
eg: She has an adventurous spirit
eg: They went on an adventurous trip through the jungle

# affectionate

pho: /əˈfek.ʃə.nət/
def: Showing love, care, or warmth toward others
eg: She gave her child an affectionate hug
eg: He is very affectionate with his family

# afraid

pho: /əˈfreɪd/
def: Feeling fear or worry about something
eg: She is afraid of flying
eg: He was afraid that he might fail

# aged

pho: /eɪdʒd/
def: Having lived for a long time; old
eg: The aged professor still taught classes well into his eighties
eg: The building looks aged and worn, its walls cracked from decades of neglect

# aggravating

pho: /ˈæɡ.rə.veɪ.tɪŋ/
def: Causing annoyance or frustration
eg: The constant noise was aggravating
eg: It’s aggravating when plans suddenly change

# aggressive

pho: /əˈɡres.ɪv/
def: Ready to attack or behave in a hostile way
def: Pursuing goals with forceful determination
eg: The dog became aggressive when a stranger approached the yard
eg: He took an aggressive approach to negotiations, refusing to compromise on price

# agile

pho: /ˈædʒ.aɪl/
def: Able to move quickly and easily
eg: The cat is agile and fast
eg: Agile teams adapt quickly to change

# agitated

pho: /ˈædʒ.ɪ.teɪ.tɪd/
def: Feeling anxious, upset, or restless
eg: She became agitated during the argument
eg: The crowd grew increasingly agitated

# agonizing

pho: /ˈæɡ.ə.naɪ.zɪŋ/
def: Causing extreme physical or emotional pain
eg: The wait for the results was agonizing
eg: He suffered agonizing back pain

# agreeable

pho: /əˈɡriː.ə.bəl/
def: Pleasant and easy to like or accept
def: Willing to agree or cooperate
eg: The weather was warm and agreeable, perfect for a picnic
eg: She said she was agreeable to changing the meeting time

# alarmed

pho: /əˈlɑːrmd/
def: Feeling frightened or worried that something bad may happen
eg: She was alarmed by the sudden noise
eg: The report left investors alarmed

# alarming

pho: /əˈlɑːr.mɪŋ/
def: Causing fear, worry, or concern
eg: The rise in drug-resistant infections is alarming to public health officials
eg: The report revealed an alarming increase in homelessness over the past year

# alert

pho: /əˈlɝːt/
def: Fully aware and paying close attention
eg: Stay alert while driving at night
eg: The guard remained alert

# alienated

pho: /ˈeɪ.li.ə.neɪ.tɪd/
def: Feeling isolated or separated from others
eg: He felt alienated at his new job
eg: The policy alienated many supporters

# alive

pho: /əˈlaɪv/
def: Living; not dead
def: Full of energy, activity, or excitement
eg: Rescuers found the hiker alive after three days in the wilderness
eg: The market comes alive at night, with vendors, music, and street food everywhere

# all

pho: /ɔːl/
def: The whole amount or every part of something
eg: All the seats were taken
eg: She spent all her money

# altruistic

pho: /ˌæl.truˈɪs.tɪk/
def: Showing concern for the well-being of others
eg: She made an altruistic donation to the food bank, refusing any public recognition for her contribution
eg: His altruistic commitment to volunteering every weekend eventually inspired his entire team to get involved

# amazing

pho: /əˈmeɪ.zɪŋ/
def: Causing great surprise or admiration
eg: The view from the mountain was amazing — we could see three countries at once
eg: She delivered an amazing performance that left the audience speechless

# ambitious

pho: /æmˈbɪʃ.əs/
def: Having a strong desire to succeed or achieve something
eg: She's ambitious enough to juggle a full-time job while finishing her degree
eg: The company has ambitious plans to expand into five new markets by next year

# ample

pho: /ˈæm.pəl/
def: More than enough; plentiful
eg: There is ample time to finish
eg: The room offers ample space

# amused

pho: /əˈmjuːzd/
def: Finding something funny or entertaining
eg: She looked amused by the joke
eg: He was amused at her reaction

# amusing

pho: /əˈmjuː.zɪŋ/
def: Causing laughter or enjoyment
eg: The mix-up over the hotel room was amusing in hindsight
eg: He told an amusing anecdote about getting lost on his first day abroad

# anchored

pho: /ˈæŋ.kɚd/
def: Firmly fixed or held in place
eg: The boat was anchored near the shore
eg: She feels anchored by her routine

# ancient

pho: /ˈeɪn.ʃənt/
def: Very old; from a long time ago
eg: They explored an ancient temple buried beneath centuries of jungle overgrowth
eg: The manuscript is so ancient that historians struggle to decipher its language

# angelic

pho: /ænˈdʒel.ɪk/
def: Extremely kind, pure, or beautiful
eg: The baby looked angelic while sleeping, her arms spread wide and her breathing perfectly quiet
eg: She has such an angelic voice that the entire hall fell silent the moment she began to sing

# angry

pho: /ˈæŋ.ɡri/
def: Feeling strong displeasure or rage
eg: He was angry about the decision to cancel the project without consulting the team
eg: She spoke in an angry tone when she realized she had been lied to

# anguished

pho: /ˈæŋ.ɡwɪʃt/
def: Experiencing severe mental or physical pain
eg: She gave an anguished cry
eg: He looked anguished after hearing the news

# animated

pho: /ˈæn.ə.meɪ.tɪd/
def: Full of life, energy, or excitement
def: Produced using animation techniques; not live-action
eg: She became animated when talking about her research, gesturing enthusiastically
eg: The film is animated, featuring hand-drawn characters inspired by Japanese folklore

# annual

pho: /ˈæn.ju.əl/
def: Occurring once every year
eg: The company holds an annual meeting to review its financial performance and set priorities for the coming year
eg: The annual charity gala raises hundreds of thousands of dollars for local schools and youth programs

# another

pho: /əˈnʌð.ɚ/
def: One more or an additional one
eg: Would you like another cup of coffee? The pot is still hot and there are biscuits left
eg: After the first strategy failed to gain traction, he tried another approach and finally broke through the problem

# antique

pho: /ænˈtiːk/
def: Old and often valuable because of its age
eg: She collects antique furniture from estate sales, carefully restoring each piece before placing it in her home
eg: The shop sells antique jewelry dating back to the Victorian era, each piece accompanied by a certificate of authenticity

# anxious

pho: /ˈæŋk.ʃəs/
def: Feeling worried, nervous, or uneasy
def: Eager or strongly wanting something to happen
eg: He felt anxious about the exam, barely sleeping the night before
eg: She was anxious to hear the results and checked her phone every few minutes

# any

pho: /ˈen.i/
def: One or some, no matter which or how many
eg: Do you have any questions?
eg: You can choose any option

# apprehensive

pho: /ˌæp.rɪˈhen.sɪv/
def: Feeling anxious or fearful about something
eg: She felt apprehensive before the interview
eg: He was apprehensive about moving abroad

# appropriate

pho: /əˈproʊ.pri.ət/
def: Suitable or proper for a particular situation
eg: That behavior is not appropriate here
eg: She chose an appropriate response

# apt

pho: /æpt/
def: Suitable or likely to do something
eg: His apt comparison between company growth and a marathon rather than a sprint resonated with the whole team
eg: Children are apt to ask many questions at once, often before the answer to the first one has been given

# arctic

pho: /ˈɑːrk.tɪk/
def: Extremely cold or relating to the North Pole region
eg: Researchers stationed in the arctic circle face temperatures that can fall below minus forty degrees
eg: The arctic wind cut through their jackets, dropping the windchill to dangerous levels within minutes of stepping outside

# arid

pho: /ˈer.ɪd/
def: Extremely dry; lacking moisture
eg: The land is so arid that farmers must rely entirely on irrigation
eg: The documentary followed explorers crossing an arid plateau with no water source for miles

# aromatic

pho: /ˌer.əˈmæt.ɪk/
def: Having a strong, pleasant smell
eg: The kitchen was filled with aromatic spices that had been toasting slowly in the pan for twenty minutes
eg: She brewed aromatic tea from dried jasmine flowers she had brought back from her trip to Morocco

# artistic

pho: /ɑːrˈtɪs.tɪk/
def: Creative or related to art
eg: He has strong artistic talent
eg: The city is known for its artistic culture

# ashamed

pho: /əˈʃeɪmd/
def: Feeling guilt or embarrassment about something
eg: She felt ashamed of her behavior
eg: He was ashamed to admit his mistake

# assured

pho: /əˈʃʊrd/
def: Confident and certain; not showing doubt or anxiety
eg: She sounded calm and assured during the press conference, despite the tough questions
eg: He gave an assured performance in his first major role, surprising even the critics

# astonishing

pho: /əˈstɑː.nɪʃ.ɪŋ/
def: Very surprising or impressive
eg: The magician’s trick was astonishing — a card appeared inside a sealed bottle that had never left the table
eg: She made astonishing progress in her first year, advancing further than most employees do in five

# athletic

pho: /æθˈlet.ɪk/
def: Strong, fit, and good at sports or physical activity
eg: He has an athletic build from years of competitive swimming and early-morning gym sessions
eg: The school encourages athletic activities by offering coaching in twelve different sports throughout the year

# attached

pho: /əˈtætʃt/
def: Joined or connected to something; emotionally close
eg: The file is attached to the email
eg: She is deeply attached to her dog

# attentive

pho: /əˈten.tɪv/
def: Paying close attention; showing care or consideration toward others
eg: The waiter was attentive, refilling glasses before anyone had to ask
eg: She listened in an attentive manner, taking notes throughout the entire lecture

# attractive

pho: /əˈtræk.tɪv/
def: Pleasing to look at or appealing
eg: The city is attractive to tourists for its blend of ancient architecture, vibrant food scene, and mild climate
eg: She has an attractive smile that puts even nervous interviewees immediately at ease

# austere

pho: /ɔːˈstɪr/
def: Very plain and without decoration or comfort
def: Strict and serious in manner or attitude
eg: The monastery had an austere design — bare stone walls and no ornaments
eg: Her austere expression made it clear she was not in the mood for small talk

# authentic

pho: /ɔːˈθen.tɪk/
def: Genuine and real; not fake or copied
eg: The painting was confirmed as authentic by three independent experts who examined its brushwork and materials
eg: She prefers authentic experiences when she travels, staying with local families rather than in hotels

# authorized

pho: /ˈɔː.θə.raɪzd/
def: Officially allowed or approved
eg: Only authorized personnel may enter
eg: She is authorized to sign the document

# automatic

pho: /ˌɔː.təˈmæt.ɪk/
def: Operating by itself with little or no human control
def: Done without conscious thought; instinctive
eg: The factory uses automatic assembly lines that require minimal supervision
eg: His response was automatic — he apologized before he even understood what had happened

# avaricious

pho: /ˌæv.əˈrɪʃ.əs/
def: Having an extreme desire for wealth or gain, even at the expense of others
eg: The avaricious landlord raised rents far beyond what tenants could afford
eg: His avaricious behavior eventually alienated even his closest business partners

# average

pho: /ˈæv.ɚ.ɪdʒ/
def: Typical or ordinary; not special
eg: Her test score was average, so the teacher suggested extra practice on the weaker topics before the final exam
eg: He is of average height for his age group but still remarkably quick on the football pitch

# aware

pho: /əˈwer/
def: Knowing or realizing something
eg: She is fully aware of the risks involved but has decided the potential benefits outweigh them
eg: He wasn’t aware of the schedule change and arrived at the old venue an hour before anyone else

# awesome

pho: /ˈɑː.səm/
def: Extremely impressive or inspiring; causing a feeling of awe
eg: The view of the canyon from the rim was truly awesome
eg: She did an awesome job pulling the event together on such short notice

# awful

pho: /ˈɑː.fəl/
def: Very bad or unpleasant; causing distress
eg: The weather was awful, with heavy rain and strong winds canceling the outdoor event
eg: He felt awful after the argument and spent the night wondering how to apologize

# awkward

pho: /ˈɑː.kwɚd/
def: Causing discomfort or embarrassment
eg: There was an awkward silence after she asked about his ex, and no one knew whether to change the subject
eg: He felt awkward at the party, not knowing anyone and unsure where to stand or what to say

# babyish

pho: /ˈbeɪ.bi.ɪʃ/
def: Behaving in a childish or immature way
eg: His babyish behavior during the meeting — interrupting, pouting, refusing to compromise — frustrated his colleagues
eg: She found the prank babyish and walked away rather than encouraging it by laughing along

# back

pho: /bæk/
def: Located behind or at the rear
eg: He sat in the back row
eg: The door is at the back of the house

# bad

pho: /bæd/
def: Not good; harmful or unpleasant
eg: Smoking is bad for your health and increases the risk of several serious conditions, including heart disease
eg: She had a particularly bad day when the presentation crashed, the client called to complain, and she missed her train home

# baggy

pho: /ˈbæɡ.i/
def: Loose and hanging in folds
eg: He showed up at the formal dinner wearing baggy jeans and a crumpled shirt, completely misjudging the dress code
eg: The sweater was so baggy that it drooped off her shoulders and the sleeves covered her hands entirely

# bare

pho: /ber/
def: Without covering, clothing, or decoration; empty or plain
eg: She walked across the bare floorboards, wincing at the cold
eg: The walls were bare except for a single faded photograph

# barren

pho: /ˈber.ən/
def: Unable to produce plants or crops; empty and without life
def: Lacking creativity, results, or usefulness
eg: The hillside was barren after the wildfire, with no vegetation for miles
eg: After months of writer's block, his mind felt barren of any good ideas

# basic

pho: /ˈbeɪ.sɪk/
def: Simple and fundamental; not advanced
eg: She learned the basic rules of the language in the first week and was having simple conversations within a month
eg: The phone had a basic design with no extra features — just a camera, speaker, and call function

# beautiful

pho: /ˈbjuː.tə.fəl/
def: Very pleasing to the senses or mind; highly attractive
eg: The sunset painted the sky in beautiful shades of orange and pink
eg: She gave a beautiful speech that moved the entire audience to tears

# belated

pho: /bɪˈleɪ.tɪd/
def: Happening later than expected
eg: Please accept my belated apology — I should have addressed this weeks ago and I regret the delay
eg: He sent a belated birthday card with a note explaining he’d been traveling and only just heard the news

# beloved

pho: /bɪˈlʌv.d/
def: Dearly loved by many people
eg: The beloved teacher retired after forty years, and former students came from across the country to say farewell
eg: The book is a beloved classic that has never gone out of print since it was first published in 1952

# beneficial

pho: /ˌben.əˈfɪʃ.əl/
def: Producing good or helpful results
eg: Regular exercise is beneficial to health
eg: The changes were beneficial for the team

# best

pho: /best/
def: Better than all others of the same kind
eg: After reviewing all the proposals, the committee agreed this was the best option within the available budget
eg: She did her best to stay calm during the debate, even when her opponent repeatedly interrupted her answers

# better

pho: /ˈbet̬.ɚ/
def: Of higher quality or more desirable than another
eg: This solution is better than the previous one
eg: He feels better today

# bewitched

pho: /bɪˈwɪtʃt/
def: Filled with delight or fascination, as if under a spell
eg: The audience was bewitched by her performance
eg: He felt bewitched by the beautiful scenery

# big

pho: /bɪɡ/
def: Large in size or amount
eg: They live in a big house on the edge of the countryside, with a wide garden that backs onto the woods
eg: He has big plans to renovate the building and convert it into a community center for local youth organizations

# big-hearted

pho: /ˌbɪɡˈhɑːr.tɪd/
def: Very kind and generous
eg: She is known for being big-hearted
eg: His big-hearted gesture touched everyone

# biodegradable

pho: /ˌbaɪ.oʊ.dɪˈɡreɪ.də.bəl/
def: Able to be broken down naturally by the environment
eg: The company switched to biodegradable packaging to reduce its environmental footprint and cut landfill waste
eg: Biodegradable materials break down in the soil without releasing harmful chemicals, unlike conventional plastics

# bite-sized

pho: /ˈbaɪt.saɪzd/
def: Small enough to be eaten in one bite
eg: She served bite-sized snacks
eg: The lesson was broken into bite-sized pieces

# bitter

pho: /ˈbɪt̬.ɚ/
def: Having a sharp, unpleasant taste or feeling
eg: The coffee tasted bitter
eg: He felt bitter about the loss

# black

pho: /blæk/
def: Having the darkest color; without light
eg: She wore a black dress to the memorial service, standing quietly near the back of the hall
eg: The sky turned black within minutes as the storm rolled in faster than anyone had predicted

# bland

pho: /blænd/
def: Lacking strong taste, flavor, or interest; dull and unstimulating
eg: The soup was bland — it needed salt, pepper, and something acidic to bring it alive
eg: He found the movie so bland that he fell asleep halfway through

# blank

pho: /blæŋk/
def: Empty or without content or expression
eg: The page was blank
eg: She gave him a blank stare

# blaring

pho: /ˈbler.ɪŋ/
def: Producing a loud, harsh, and overwhelming sound
eg: Music was blaring from the car parked outside, making it impossible to sleep
eg: The alarm was blaring in the hallway, sending everyone rushing toward the exits

# bleak

pho: /bliːk/
def: Cold, empty, or without hope
eg: The landscape looked bleak after the harvest — bare fields, grey sky, and no sign of life for miles in any direction
eg: The future seemed bleak for the small town after the factory closed and most working families began to leave

# blind

pho: /blaɪnd/
def: Unable to see or lacking awareness
eg: He is blind in one eye
eg: She was blind to the danger

# blissful

pho: /ˈblɪs.fəl/
def: Full of perfect happiness and joy
eg: They spent a blissful afternoon in the countryside, completely free from stress
eg: She felt blissful on vacation, having forgotten all about work deadlines

# blond

pho: /blɑːnd/
def: Having light-colored hair
eg: He has short blond hair that turns noticeably lighter during summer from spending long hours outdoors
eg: The blond child smiled shyly and hid behind his mother when the photographer tried to take his picture

# blue

pho: /bluː/
def: Having the color of the clear sky or sea
def: Feeling sad or depressed
eg: She wore a blue jacket that matched the color of the ocean behind her
eg: He's been feeling blue ever since his best friend moved away

# blushing

pho: /ˈblʌʃ.ɪŋ/
def: Turning red in the face from embarrassment or emotion
eg: She gave a blushing smile when her name was called out in front of the whole class as the top student
eg: He stood there blushing when the whole office sang happy birthday to him completely out of nowhere

# bogus

pho: /ˈboʊ.ɡəs/
def: False or fake; not genuine
eg: The claim turned out to be bogus
eg: He was arrested for selling bogus tickets

# boiling

pho: /ˈbɔɪ.lɪŋ/
def: Extremely hot or showing strong emotion
eg: The water is boiling
eg: She was boiling with anger

# bold

pho: /boʊld/
def: Confident and willing to take risks; not afraid to show your views
def: (Of text or design) strong and visually striking
eg: She made the bold decision to quit her job and start her own company
eg: The poster's bold colors and thick fonts grabbed attention from across the room

# bony

pho: /ˈboʊ.ni/
def: Very thin or having prominent bones
eg: The stray dog looked bony and underfed, its ribs clearly visible through its matted and dull fur
eg: He has such a bony frame that the tailor had to add extra padding to the shoulders of the suit jacket

# boring

pho: /ˈbɔːr.ɪŋ/
def: Not interesting or exciting; dull and tedious
eg: The lecture was so boring that half the students were checking their phones
eg: He found the movie boring — two hours of slow dialogue and no real conflict

# bossy

pho: /ˈbɑː.si/
def: Always telling others what to do
eg: She sounded bossy during the meeting
eg: His bossy attitude annoyed people

# both

pho: /boʊθ/
def: Referring to two things together
eg: Both options are acceptable, but the second one is significantly cheaper and easier to implement
eg: They both agreed that the project needed more preparation time before it could be presented to the board

# bouncy

pho: /ˈbaʊn.si/
def: Full of energy; able to bounce
eg: The ball was so bouncy that it flew off the court whenever the children hit it even slightly too hard
eg: She walked with a bouncy step that matched her mood — clearly something very good had happened

# bountiful

pho: /ˈbaʊn.tɪ.fəl/
def: Large in quantity; plentiful
eg: The harvest was bountiful that year, with enough surplus for the community to donate to several regional food banks
eg: They enjoyed a bountiful meal that covered the entire table, with dish after dish brought out from the kitchen

# bowed

pho: /baʊd/
def: Bent or curved downward under pressure or weight
eg: The old man walked with a bowed back, hunched from decades of labor
eg: The tree branches were bowed under the weight of the heavy snow

# brave

pho: /breɪv/
def: Showing courage and strength in difficult or dangerous situations
eg: The firefighter was brave enough to enter the burning building without hesitation
eg: She made the brave choice to speak out, even knowing it would cost her the promotion

# breakable

pho: /ˈbreɪ.kə.bəl/
def: Able to be broken easily
eg: The glass figurine was clearly breakable, so she wrapped it in layers of tissue paper before placing it in the box
eg: These items are clearly marked breakable on the outside of the packaging, so handle with extreme care

# brief

pho: /briːf/
def: Short in time or length
eg: He gave a brief explanation before handing out the worksheets, leaving the rest of the session for practice
eg: The meeting was surprisingly brief — just twenty minutes to cover three agenda items and reassign outstanding tasks

# bright

pho: /braɪt/
def: Giving off a lot of light or showing intelligence
eg: The sun was bright enough to make reading outside uncomfortable without sunglasses
eg: She’s a bright student who grasps new concepts quickly and often helps classmates with the trickier problems

# brilliant

pho: /ˈbrɪl.jənt/
def: Extremely clever or impressive
eg: That was a brilliant idea — simple enough to implement immediately and exactly what the client had been asking for
eg: The sky looked brilliant at sunset, streaked with deep orange and vivid pink above the horizon

# brisk

pho: /brɪsk/
def: Quick and energetic
eg: She took a brisk walk around the park every morning before work, covering three kilometers in under thirty minutes
eg: The morning air was brisk enough to make her breath visible, so she zipped her jacket all the way up

# broken

# good

pho: /ɡʊd/
def: Having positive qualities; satisfactory
eg: She’s a genuinely good person who donates her spare time to the local youth center without expecting anything in return
eg: The food tastes surprisingly good for a place that looks like a roadside diner from the outside

# good-natured

pho: /ˌɡʊdˈneɪ.tʃɚd/
def: Kind, friendly, and patient
eg: He’s a good-natured man who manages to stay pleasant even after a hard day and a long commute
eg: Her good-natured smile relaxed everyone in the waiting room, turning an anxious atmosphere into a calm one

# gorgeous

pho: /ˈɡɔːr.dʒəs/
def: Extremely beautiful or attractive
eg: She looked gorgeous in that dress — the deep blue matched her eyes perfectly, and every head turned when she entered
eg: The view from the top was absolutely gorgeous — rolling hills bathed in late afternoon light stretching to the horizon

# graceful

pho: /ˈɡreɪs.fəl/
def: Moving or behaving with smooth, elegant ease
eg: She’s a graceful dancer whose movements look effortless even when the routine is complex
eg: The swan was graceful as it glided across the still surface of the lake

# gracious

pho: /ˈɡreɪ.ʃəs/
def: Polite, kind, and generous
eg: She was gracious to every guest, taking time to greet each person individually and making them feel genuinely welcome
eg: He gave a gracious reply to the criticism, acknowledging the valid points and thanking the reviewer for their feedback

# grand

pho: /ɡrænd/
def: Large, impressive, or important
eg: A grand building dominated the central square, its columns and carved stonework a reminder of the city’s imperial past
eg: They held a grand celebration to mark the company’s centenary, filling the opera house with guests from every era of its history

# grandiose

pho: /ˈɡræn.di.oʊs/
def: Impressively large or elaborate, often to an excessive or pretentious degree
eg: He came up with a grandiose plan to build the world’s tallest skyscraper in five years
eg: His speech was grandiose, full of sweeping promises that had no concrete backing

# granular

pho: /ˈɡræn.jə.lɚ/
def: Composed of small particles
eg: Granular sand covered the beach in a fine layer, warm to the touch and sparkling in the afternoon sun
eg: The material has a granular texture that gives it grip on wet surfaces and makes it ideal for outdoor use

# grateful

pho: /ˈɡreɪt.fəl/
def: Feeling thankful
eg: I’m deeply grateful for your help during one of the most difficult weeks I’ve had in years
eg: She felt genuinely grateful to be safe after the car broke down in a remote area and a stranger stopped to help

# grave

pho: /ɡreɪv/
def: Serious or solemn
eg: Ignoring the warning signs turned out to be a grave mistake that cost the project months of rework
eg: He spoke in a grave tone when he told the team that the deadline could not be extended under any circumstances

# gray

pho: /ɡreɪ/
def: Having a color between black and white
eg: Gray clouds filled the sky by mid-morning, and within an hour the first drops of rain had started to fall
eg: He wore a gray jacket over a plain white shirt — understated and professional without trying too hard

# great

pho: /ɡreɪt/
def: Very good or impressive; of notable quality or magnitude
def: Very large in degree or extent
eg: She did a great job organizing the conference with a team of only three people
eg: The discovery was a great achievement that changed how scientists think about the brain

# greedy

pho: /ˈɡriː.di/
def: Wanting more than needed
eg: He’s greedy for attention and manages to redirect almost every conversation back to himself within minutes
eg: She has such a greedy appetite that she finished her plate, then helped herself to what her brother had left

# green

pho: /ɡriːn/
def: Having the color of grass; inexperienced
eg: Green leaves appeared on the branches almost overnight once the temperature climbed above ten degrees
eg: She’s still green at the job but shows real potential and asks exactly the right questions

# gregarious

pho: /ɡrɪˈɡer.i.əs/
def: Sociable, outgoing, and enjoying the company of others
eg: He’s so gregarious that he strikes up a conversation with anyone who sits near him
eg: Her gregarious personality made her a natural fit for a career in sales

# grim

pho: /ɡrɪm/
def: Serious, depressing, or unpleasant
eg: Grim news arrived just as the team was about to begin the morning briefing — the funding had been cut entirely
eg: He wore a grim expression throughout the meeting, which made everyone nervous about what was coming next

# grimy

pho: /ˈɡraɪ.mi/
def: Covered with dirt or grime; unpleasantly dirty
eg: The mechanic’s grimy hands left smears on everything he touched
eg: The walls were grimy from years of cooking fumes and neglect

# gripping

pho: /ˈɡrɪp.ɪŋ/
def: Holding your attention completely; exciting and hard to stop reading or watching
eg: The novel is a gripping thriller that kept me reading until two in the morning
eg: The match was so gripping that none of the spectators moved from their seats

# grizzled

pho: /ˈɡrɪz.əld/
def: Having gray or white hair
eg: A grizzled veteran sat at the bar, nursing a drink and telling stories to anyone willing to listen
eg: His beard looked grizzled and unkempt, as if he’d spent the past two weeks camping without a razor

# gross

pho: /ɡroʊs/
def: Unpleasant or excessive
eg: That smell coming from the fridge is absolutely gross — something has been in there far too long
eg: Saying she never listens is a gross exaggeration — she just processes things differently and tends to respond later

# grotesque

pho: /ɡroʊˈtesk/
def: Extremely ugly or distorted
eg: A grotesque statue guarded the entrance to the cemetery, its features twisted and weathered beyond recognition
eg: The scene was grotesque — a combination of violence and chaos that left the investigators shaken for days

# grouchy

pho: /ˈɡraʊ.tʃi/
def: Irritable or bad-tempered
eg: He’s grouchy in the mornings and communicates mainly in grunts until his second cup of coffee
eg: A grouchy reply from the receptionist set the tone for what turned out to be a frustrating visit

# grounded

pho: /ˈɡraʊn.dɪd/
def: Sensible, realistic, and not easily influenced by status or fame
def: (Of a plane, pilot, or child) prevented from traveling or going out
eg: Despite her success, she’s surprisingly grounded and easy to talk to
eg: All flights were grounded due to the severe storm moving across the region

# growing

pho: /ˈɡroʊ.ɪŋ/
def: Increasing in size, number, or importance over time
eg: There is a growing concern among doctors about the overuse of antibiotics
eg: The company serves a growing customer base that expanded by 40% last year

# growling

pho: /ˈɡraʊ.lɪŋ/
def: Making a low, rough sound
eg: The dog was growling at the stranger at the gate, low and steady, a clear warning to come no closer
eg: A growling engine echoed through the tunnel as the old locomotive came slowly into the station

# grown

pho: /ɡroʊn/
def: Fully developed; adult
eg: She has grown children now, which still surprises her — she says she keeps expecting to see the toddlers she remembers
eg: The plant is fully grown and has outgrown its pot, sending roots through the drainage holes at the base

# grubby

pho: /ˈɡrʌb.i/
def: Dirty or untidy
eg: Grubby hands had left marks all over the glass door, a sure sign the children had been through recently
eg: He wore a grubby shirt that should have gone in the wash three days ago, but he had run out of clean ones

# gruesome

pho: /ˈɡruː.səm/
def: Extremely unpleasant or horrifying

eg: The movie had gruesome scenes that weren’t necessary for the story and seemed included purely for shock value

# grumpy

pho: /ˈɡrʌm.pi/
def: Easily annoyed or irritated

eg: A grumpy response followed every suggestion, which made the brainstorming session feel pointless and draining

# guilty

pho: /ˈɡɪl.ti/
def: Feeling responsible for wrongdoing
eg: She felt guilty about lying for days afterward and eventually told the truth just to stop the feeling
eg: A guilty expression crossed his face the moment the wallet was mentioned, confirming what everyone had already suspected

# gullible

pho: /ˈɡʌl.ə.bəl/
def: Easily tricked or deceived
eg: He’s too gullible to work in sales — he accepts every excuse at face value and rarely follows up
eg: Gullible people often believe rumors without checking the source, which is how misinformation spreads so quickly

# gummy

pho: /ˈɡʌm.i/
def: Sticky or chewy
eg: Gummy candy stuck to his teeth the moment he bit into it, making him regret the choice immediately
eg: The texture felt gummy and unpleasant, more like chewing glue than eating the dish she had been described

# hairy

pho: /ˈher.i/
def: Covered with hair; frightening or risky
eg: A hairy, unkempt dog bolted across the road, nearly causing two cyclists to swerve
eg: That situation was hairy — three suppliers had failed to deliver and the launch was just forty-eight hours away

# half

pho: /hæf/
def: One of two equal parts
eg: Half the cake was gone by the time the birthday girl arrived, which caused a tense conversation with her older brother
eg: She’s half awake during morning meetings and always asks to review the minutes before making any decisions

# handmade

pho: /ˌhændˈmeɪd/
def: Made by hand, not by machine
eg: She sold handmade jewelry at the weekend market, each piece crafted from locally sourced silver and gemstones
eg: The table is handmade from reclaimed wood, and no two pieces in the set are exactly the same

# handsome

pho: /ˈhæn.səm/
def: Attractive or good-looking, especially with a strong, well-defined appearance
def: (Of an amount) large and impressive
eg: He’s often described as handsome — tall, well-dressed, and confident
eg: A handsome reward was offered to anyone who could locate the stolen painting

# handy

pho: /ˈhæn.di/
def: Useful or convenient
eg: This folding tool is incredibly handy when you’re camping — it combines six functions in a single pocket-sized device
eg: He’s handy with repairs and has fixed every appliance in the house rather than calling someone out

# happy

pho: /ˈhæp.i/
def: Feeling pleasure or contentment
eg: She feels genuinely happy today for the first time in months, and it shows in the way she carries herself
eg: That was a genuinely happy moment — everyone in the room was smiling and no one wanted it to end

# happy-go-lucky

# hard

pho: /hɑːrd/

# harmful

# hasty

pho: /ˈheɪ.sti/

# hateful
